Survey Report for the SEDCO 703 Rig Move to
the Corallina # 2 ( A ) and Corallina # 3 ( B ) Locations



ABSTRACT

Between 9 and 18 March 1998 Fugro Survey Pty Ltd provided equipment and personnel for
the Sedco 703 rig move from the Laminaria # 5 location to the Corallina # 2 ( A ) and Corallina # 3 ( B )
locations . These sites are both situated in the Timor Sea within Permit Area ACL5

approximately 320 nautical miles West North West of Darwin .

The Sedco 703 was successfully located within the specified position tolerances using DGPS . A
position check was provided post positioning by static GPS observations . Temporary Guide
Bases ( TGB ) for each location were successfully positioned using transponders on the TGB and
the existing seabed transponder array at Corallina . The final positions for the TGBs at Corallir
# 2 ( A ) and Corallina # 3 ( B ) were determined as :

Corallina # 2 ( A ) Corallina # 3 ( B )

Easting 167 280.0 mE Easting 167 268.4 mE
Northing 8 827 430.3 mN Northing 8 827 382.8 mN
Latitude 10035 33.628 South Latitude 107 35 35.168 South

Longitude 58125057 35.233 East Longitude 58 8125257 34.836 East

Rig Heading 213.4 True Rig Heading 213.5 True
TGB Heading 213.7 ? True TGB Heading 2715.8 True

The position for the TGB at Corallina # 2 ( A ) is 1.6m @ 225.6 ? ( True ) from the intended location
for the Corallina # 2 ( A ) drill hole . The TGB at Corallina # 2 ( A ) was placed on the seabed at
approximately 2000hrs on 120398 with its position determined by 2100hrs .

The position for the TGB at Corallina # 3 ( B ) is 0.5m @ 292.4 ? ( True ) from the intended location

for the Corallina # 3 ( B ) drill hole . The TGB at Corallina # 3 ( B was placed on the seabed at
approximately 0440hrs on 160398 with its position determined by 0630hrs .

1.0 . INTRODUCTION

Fugro Survey Pty Ltd ( Fugro ) was contracted by Woodside Offshore Petroleum Pty Ltd
( Woodside ) to provide positioning services for the move of the drilling rig Sedco 703 from

the Laminaria # 5 location to the Corallina # 2 ( A ) and the Corallina # 3 ( B ) locations in the

Timor Sea offshore North Western Australia . A location diagram is shown as Figure 1

overleaf .

The following report details the equipment used the survey parameters the survey

procedures and the results of the survey . A section on safety is also included .

1.1 Scope of Work

Personnel and equipment were to be provided on a 24 hour basis for :

Surface Navigation for the Sedco 703 and the two anchor handling tug
( AHT ) boats the Lady Audrey and Lady Elaine using Fugros Starfix
Differential GPS and Wide Area Differential GPS systems .

Remote tug tracking and anchor handling for both AHTs using Fugros
PCBarge software and radiomodem system .

Subsurface positioning of each TGB using Woodsides Sonardyne long
baseline ( LBL ) acoustic equipment . Fugro were also tasked with the
calibration of the ROV underwater gyro compass which was used to obtain
heading of the TGB .

Position check calculation for the Corallina # 2 ( A ) and Corallina # 3 ( B )
locations using GPS static baseline observations on the Sedco 703 and at

two locations ashore .

Processing and reporting were also included as part of the scope of work .

Proposed location for the Sedco 703 and associated anchors were provided by
Woodside .

3.2 Equipment Descriptions

3.2.1 Positioning System OmniSTARStarfix ll DGPS and WADS

HY1324437908em

Fugro Surveys OmniSTAR and Starfix I DGPS systems were installed on
the Sedco 703 where they provided the primary system for navigation .
Differential corrections were received from four permanent reference
stations at Perth Karratha Darwin and Bali to produce a wide area
solution for vessel position to an accuracy of better than 2m . Corrections
were received via both the OmniSTAR and Starfix il systems the former
using a whip antenna to receive signals from the Optus satellite and the
later a standard Mdome locked to the Inmarsat Indian Ocean Regi .
( IOR ) satellite .

OmniSTAR and Starfix Il are networks of Differential GPS reference
stations located throughout Australia New Zealand and South East Asia
providing GPS satellite position corrections to mobile stations via a
Network Control Centre ( NCC ) located in Perth Australia . Corrections are
processed and checked before transmission to users at an update rate of 2
seconds or less . The Starfix Il network provides differential coverage over
the entire South East Asian Australian and New Zealand regions via the
Inmarsat Indian Ocean Region ( IOR ) and Pacific Ocean Region ( POR )
satellites whilst OmniSTAR covers Australia and New Zealand via tf
Optus Satellite .

Tweive channel GPS receivers operate at each reference station on a UPS
system and mains power with an autostart generator as backup for
prolonged power outages . A 10046 backup system is mobilised in an
operationally ready state that can be remotely switched on from the NCC .

Reference stations are routinely checked and monitored .

The NCC is located at Fugro Surveys Perth office and manned on a 24
hour per day basis . The centre utilises full system redundancy on a UPS

system and mains power with an autostart backup generator for

Page 7

-----Page 22-----

Prepared for Woodside Offshore Petroleum Pty Ltd GRO

Survey Report for the SEDCO 703 Rig Move to
the Corallina # 2 ( A ) and Corallina # 3 ( B ) Locations



3.2.2

prolonged power outages . The NCC continually receives and monitors
signals from the reference stations processes the received data and then
transmits DGPS corrections in the form of pseudorange corrections to the
satellite uplink for broadcast to users mobile receivers . If there is an
equipment failure or malfunction at any reference station an alarm at the
NCC notifies the operator and backup equipment can then be switched

into operation until an engineer can arrive on site .

The system can be operated on userselect single reference station
positioning with an accuracy of 35 metres or multiple reference station
network positioning ( Wide Area DGPS ) with accuracy of 2 metres or less
while dual online system redundancy provides for an overall system
reliability in the order of 99.9746 . Wide Area Differential GPS ( WADGPS )
proprietary software utilises multiple reference station corrections to
increase position accuracy and network reliability using the Wide Area
Differential Solution ( WADS ) multistation muitibaseline network . The
effect to the positioning accuracy of droppingout a reference station in the
network is minimal when operating WADGPS .

DGPS has operated successfully with only minor interruptions ( such as
satellite maintenance and constellation reconfiguration ) since first being
commissioned in 1986 . With an operating satellite constellation of 21
satellites little or no positioning interruptions are experienced in current

conditions .

Navigation Computer System PCNav

PCNav is a Fugro Survey internally developed navigation and data logging
system which includes software hardware peripherals and all interfacing
cables required for realtime navigation and data logging . The system is
based on an IBM compatible personnel computer ( PC ) with a 486
processor and maths coprocessor VGA graphics and a hard disk .

HY1324437908em

Page 8

-----Page 23-----

Prepared for Woodside Offshore Petroleum Pty Ltd fes R O
Surey Report for the SEDCO 703 Rig Move to HES
the Corallina # 2 ( A ) and Corallina # 3 ( B ) Locations ARN

Interfacing to various navigation systems is via the PC serial card which
also enables a variety of configurable ASCII outputs to other programs or
logging devices .

PCNav allows a maximum of 8 LOPs from a RangeRange system and will
compute vessel position and quality of fix using the Variation of
Coordinates Least Squares calculation technique . The software will also
accept 2 LOPs in the form of a range and bearing or coordinates from
devices such as a GPS receiver or WADGPS computer . The calculated
position is then displayed on a graphics screen relative to defined
Runlines Waypoints Centrelines files and Databases .

Position and depth data can be output to a printer and is logged to the
computer hard disk for subsequent processing .

The key features of the system are :

Realtime updates

Simultaneous high resolution soundings at 10sec
Remote helimsmans colour graphic display

Colour graphic display

Extensive offline calculation packages

Uses centrelines runlines waypoints and databases
Baseline crossings and insitu calibration routines .
Full logging of essential data or all raw data

Individual weighting of LOPs

Fixed memory filter and acoustic range data

Printer output sent to logging file for reporting

Display of vessel shape

Mouse or keyboard driven

Input of runline centreline and waypoint libraries
Display of databases coastline and feature files

Online interface test facility

3.2.3

The program was used on the Sedco 703 to display and log the position of
the rig and show its relationship to features such as existing pipelines
anchor positions and target locations .

A remote monitor was provided for use by the Helmsman .

PCBarge

Fugro Surveys own PCBarge software was used on the Sedco 703 for
anchor handling purposes .

PC Barge is a real time vessel tracking management system developed by
Fugro Survey and designed to remotely control up to four vessels using

packet data transferred on radio modems .

The overall configuration was a PCNav computer on the Sedco 703 linked
to the PCBarge computer which managed the other PCNav systems
installed on the remote AHTs to be tracked i.e the Lady Elaine and the
Lady Audrey .

The use of PCNav on the remote vessels allows for any standard
positioning system and auxiliary equipment to be interfaced with all the
normal navigation functions such as runlines and waypoints . By allowing
these vessels to run an independent system there is no loss of positioning

even if radio communications are poor or interrupted .

Sv ? S Velocity Probe

An Applied Microsystems SV velocity probe was provided so that the

velocity of sound in the water column could be observed and measured

and used in the Sonardyne LBL system controller . The SV ? is a

miniaturised sound velocity probe specifically designed to enable

HY1324437908em

Page 11

-----Page 26-----

Prepared for Woodside Offshore Petroleum Pty Ltd GRO

Survey Report for the SEDCO 703 Rig Move to NG 22
the Corallina # 2 ( A ) and Corallina # 3 ( B ) Locations F7 aaa

3.2.5

3.2.6

calibration of an echo sounder or acoustic array or other subsea equipment

where knowledge of the velocity of sound is essential .

The probe is lightweight and easily deployed by hand using a reel of rope
to lower the unit to the seabed . Lowered from the vessel the solid state
probe records start time sound velocity pressure ( depth ) and temperature
into the probes internal memory . A builtin microprocessor and program
enable samples to be logged at user defined depth intervals on the way
down and at every change in sound velocity on the way back up . The
probe quickly and accurately measures and records a precisely digitised
sound velocity profile of the water column using a singaround velocity
sensor . It should be noted that the velocity of sound is measured directly
and not caiculated .

Once recovered to the surface data was downloaded onto the PC then
analysed using the VEL program to determine the correct scaling of the
raw observed acoustic ranges .

Gyrocompass

A Tokimec GM 2021 gyrocompass was interfaced to the PCNav computer
to enable the vessels orientation to be displayed at all times . The heading
data was also used in the computation of offset positions from the vessel

datum point .

OmniSTAR plus Enhanced Differential System ( EDS )

The OmniSTAR plus Enhanced Differential System is a combined 8
channel GPS receiver and WADS Differential correction receiver
processor packaged together with an Intel based single board computer

in one compact lightweight unit .

Enhanced corrections specific to the user location are produced based on
the data received from multiple reference stations and these corrections
are passed to the GPS receiver . Corrected position is then output to the

navigation computer .

Only one antenna is required for both the GPS and the OmniSTAR
differential signals .

Fluxgate KVH 1000

Fluxgate KVH compasses were installed aboard each of the AHTs

provide vessel heading to the navigation computer .
The compass is comprised of a display unit and remote sensor . The
sensor measures the earths magnetic field tot 1 ? and outputs are stable

accurate and instantly responsive to a change in vessel heading .

The compasses are calibrated by the vessel making two 360 turns .

Each baseline was observed in both directions except for TP110 to TP007 where
only one baseline direction was observed . The velocity of sound for each baseline
in the above table was derived from the reported ranges . The velocity as

measured by the SV 8 instrument was 1495.3 ms

The sound velocity discrepancy observed on the longest baseline is attributed to
two factors firstly movement of the transponders and secondly attenuation of the
sound signals over distances greater than 1000m .

None of the seabed transponders appear to have significantly moved since their
installation in October 1997 . Included in Appendix E are notes on the current
battery levels of the array transponders .

5.1

5.2

5.0 . SURVEY PROCEDURES

Mobilisation

The equipment required for the project is listed in section 3.1 . Most of the survey
equipment is mounted into a purpose built rack on the bridge of the Sedco 703 .
For the acoustic work an extra laptop computer to process the acoustic data was
mobilised along with the PAN unit on the bridge . The dunking transducer was
deployed from the life boat station .

A replacement computer and monitor were sent to replace the faulty equipmer

which was returned to Perth during the previous rig move .

On arrival on the Sedco 703 ali personnel attended a rig inductionsafety overview

meeting .

The Lady Audery and Lady Elaine were already mobilised from a previous rig
move . However checks to the Lady Audreys system uncovered a fauity radio

whip antenna . The antenna was replaced with the spare onboard the Sedco 703 .

General Survey Procedures

Before the move the coordinates for the Corallina # 2 ( A ) and Corallina # Z ( E .
locations were checked using the PCNav navigation software verifying the
W6884 to AGD84 transformation and the geographical to grid conversion . A copy
of the PCNav software configuration is included in Appendix C .

Coordinates for the intended anchor pattern were also calculated from the
bearing and chain length data supplied by Sedco Forex . Anchor and waypoint
files were then generated for display on the navigation monitors aboard the rig and
AHTs .

The final anchor drop coordinates are included in Section 6.2 .

HY1324437908em Paga 17

-----Page 36-----

Prepared for Woodside Offshore Petroleum Pty Ltd GRO
Survey Report for the SEDCO 703 Rig Move to NG
the Corallina # 2 ( A ) and Corallina # 3 ( B ) Locations PEG

Recovery of Anchors at the Laminaria # 5 Location

Anchor recovery operations at Laminaria # 5 commenced at 0330 on 110398 .
Each AHT was given a runline approximating the length and bearing of its
assigned anchor . The AHT then followed this runline after the pennant chain
chaser ( PCC ) had been passed from the rig until it arrived at the anchor . Once
the anchor had been broken out the AHT followed the runline back to the Sedco
703 .

The order in which the anchors were recovered was 1 5 8 4 7 3 2 and 6 . Once
anchor 6 had been passed to the rig the Lady Audery was given anchor 2 and
joined the Lady Elaine who had anchor 3 in towing the rig to the Corallina # 2 ( A )

location .

Bringing the Sedco 703 onto Location

At approximately 1.5 nM from location the AHT on anchor 2 passed the anchor
back to the rig and proceeded to pick up anchor 7 . Once anchor 7 was passed the
lead tug continued the tow towards Corallina # 2 ( A ) . The trailing AHT on anchor 7

held position 200m from the drop position until the rig was over location .

Once the rig was over the target location at 2330 on 110398 anchor 7 was
lowered to the seabed . A runline to each subsequent target drop ccordinate was
displayed on the AHT navigation system . When the desired length of anchor chain
had been paid out the anchor was lowered to the seabed . The AHT would the
follow the runline back to the Sedco 703 and pass over the PCC . All the primary
anchors ( 7263 ) were deployed by 0441 on 120398 . All secondary anchors
( 8415 ) were deployed by 1202 on 120398 . Pretensioning of the rigs anchors

was done following deployment of the final anchor .

Once pretensioning was complete the rig moved over the Corallina # 2 ( A ) target
coordinate and the TGB was prepared for deployment . Two transponders were

attached to the TGB centreline one aft 2.65m and one forward 2.65m from the

HY1324437908em Page 18

-----Page 37-----

Prepared for Woodside Offshore Petroleum Pty Ltd
Survey Report for the SEDCO 703 Rig Move to
the Corallina # 2 ( A ) and Corallina # 3 ( B ) Locations





5.3

TGB centre . Refer to Figure 8 for a diagram of the transponder offsets on the
TGB .

Once the TGB was on the seabed acoustic baselines were read giving the final
coordinate for the TGB transponder . If the TGB was found to be outside the 3m
tolerance circle then the TGB was to be repositioned . The orientation of the TGB
was observed using the ROV underwater gyro and compared with the baseline
between the 2 TGB transponders . The mean of the transponder positions gave a
coordinate for the centre of the TGB .

With the TGB in position 1 hours DGPS data was gathered as well as 6 hou
Static GPS baseline data to check the surface position of the rig . A final
orientation of the TGB was determined following the installation of the RGB .

This was repeated when the rig moved on anchors over to the Corallina # 3 ( B )
target coordinate .

Demobilisation
Personnel left the Sedco 703 on 18 March 1998 and returned to Perth on the

same day . Data from the Darwin reference stations were collected and hand
carried back to Perth .

6.3

Corallina # 2 ( A ) Static Baseline GPS Positioning
Survey Method

GPS Phase data was logged for approximately a 6 hr period using Trimble
4000SSE receivers . Data was logged at 15 second epochs and a mask angle of
10 ? on the Sedco 703 rig and at two shore control stations in the Darwin area . The
two Darwin stations are :

1 ) Survey House 14 Shepherd Street Darwin
2 ) WINN BM4563

This enabled 2 static baselines to be observed from the shore control points to the
antenna on the rig . The results from the static baselines were then used in a

network solution to provide the final static baseline position for the antenna .

The drill stem position was then calculated using the antennas offsets and

observed rig heading .

6.4 Differential GPS Positioning

Survey Method

A position for the drill stem on the Sedco 703 was determined using the mean
position from 1 hr of Differential GPS data . Data was logged at 30 second
intervals . The Antenna 1 position is the permanent GPS antenna position . The
PCNav system computes the coordinate for the drill stem position based on the
antennas known offsets from the drill string and the calibrated gyro heading .

Corallina # 2 ( A ) Results

The derived coordinates for the drill stem were averaged for the observation
period to give the following results .

6.5 Temporary Guide Base Positioning

It was required to determine the position of the Temporary Guide Base ( TGB ) at
the Laminaria drill hole location . Please refer overleaf to Figure 8. showing
transponder location . The position for the T.G.B . is regarded as the final drilling
location for the Corallina # 2 ( A ) and Corallina # 3 ( B ) wells .

Survey Method

The observation procedure required the following steps :

. Checking the integrity of the seabed array . This was accomplished by
comparing the current baseline ranges to the ranges reported following
installation of the array . The Corallina array coordinates are listed in
section .

Observing a sound velocity profile to determine the mean velocity of sound
for the water column and at seabed . The mean value observed was used
to correctiy scale all observed ranges between the dunking transducer and
the TGB transponder . This mean velocity was used solely during relay
mode operations . A graph showing the sound velocity profile is shown in
Figure 9 overleaf .

7.0 SAFETY

All work during the project was conducted within the guidelines of Fugro Surveys Safety
Policy as defined in Fugro Surveys Safety Manual ( Doc FSSM01 ) .

Al ! Fugro personnel had undergone a Fugro Survey general safety induction at Fugros
Perth office and completed helicopter ditching and offshore survival courses ( HUET ) .
Relevant documentation is available from the Fugro Survey safety officer in the Perth

office .

A copy of Fugro Surveys safety manual ( Doc FSSM01 ) and offshore Survey Safety
Practices ( Doc FSSM06 ) were available on site .

Fugro personnel attended the Sedco 703 induction upon arrival onboard the Sedco 703 .
An abandon vessel drill was staged on 120398 . A weekly safety meeting held on
150398 for all rigs personnel was also attended by the survey personnel .

Personal safety equipment was worn as required .

No incidents or injuries involving Fugro personnel were reported .

Prepared for Woodside Offshore Petroleum Pty Ltd fueeo
Survey Report for the SEDCO 703 Rig Move to er CZ
the Corallina # 2 ( A ) and Corallina # 3 ( 8 ) Locations PIN

8.0 . CONCLUSIONS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
1 . All navigation equipment worked well and as expected .

2 . The current transponders onboard the Sedco 703 are of an older style and can not
perform the fast simultaneous function . This means that to position a transponder
on the TGB each individual baseline to the array transponders must be read
separately . This takes time and is for all practical considerations meaningless
while the 7GB is off the seabed . The fast simultaneous transponders would be
well suited to this type of work as meaningful position fixes on the TGB could be
made whilst the TGB was off the seabed .

3 . A faulty radio whip antenna and 12V power supply were hand carried to Perth and

will need to be replaced before the next rig move .

LAMINARIA # 5 PRE RIG MOVE GYRO CALIBRATION

Abstract :

References :

Method :

M. Lu su Surveyor . Verified and checkedby : S. Dykes

A calibration of the survey gyro compass was carried out by sun azimuth on 10 ?
March 1998 . A correction value of 71.7 ? was present in the PCNav system during
the calibration . A difference of 0.5 ? was observed and applied giving a new

correction value of 71.2 .

Survey Report for the Sedco 703 Rig Move to the Laminaria # 5 Location
Fugro Survey Sunshot Computer Program

All computer clocks and wrist watches were synchronised to UTC time prior to the
observations . A theodolite was then setup on the helideck and obsevations made
to the vessel ! reference ( RO ) which is at 180 to the rig heading . 3 sets of
obeservations were made between this point and the sun . The results are tabulated

below .

SperrySun Drilling Services

INTRODUCTION

SperrySun Drilling Services Insite Mudlogging Unit was contracted to assist Woodside
Offshore Petroleum during the drilling of Corallina2 from the Sedco 703 Semi Submersible

located in the Timor Sea permit ACL5 .
The service commenced from spud on the 12 ! of March 1998 to TD of the 8 12 section at
3622m MD 3332.9m TVD on the 11th of 1998 . It was temporarily suspended between 15 to

30 March when the rig was winched to Corallina 3 .

This report is intended as a summary of the information and data collected monitored and

analysed as part of the service . The work was carried out by the following engineers .

DATA ENGINEERS LOGGING ENGINEERS.77 SAMPLE CATCHERS

Ariel B. Bautista Penelope Allen
Huw HughesJones Elizabeth Derrington
Alan Schutt Paul Tsang
Mario Shelford John Rampton

End of Well Report Corallina2 1

SperrySun Drilling Services

SYNOPSIS

Corillina2 was spudded on the 12 March 1998 at 23:45 from the Sedco 703 Semi
Submersible drilling rg . A Varei L3A Tricone bit spudded in at 438.0 m RKGB and drilled to
490.0 m at an average penetration rate of 51mhr . A Totco survey taken at section TD gave a
hole angle of 2 degrees . 3020 casing couldnt be seated so a hole opener was run into the
36 hole to reduce the hole angle which was measured at 0.4 degrees . Returns were
circulated to the seabed . The 30x20 casing was set and cemented at a depth of 484 m. The
17 2 hole section was drilled with a Security SS3ISGJ4 from 490 m to 895 m without
incident at an average rate of 85 mhr . The 13 38 casing was successfully run and cemented

with the shoe depth at 890m . The rig was then skidded over to Corallina3 on 15 March .

The rig was skidded back to Corallina2 on the 30 ! March 1998 with the BOPs and Riser
suspended below the rig . Bit # 4 a Reed MHP 11G was run in hole on 31 March and tagged
cement at 845 m. A leak off test was performed at 897m the results of which gave an
equivalent mud weight of 1.43 sg . Drilling continued from 897m using sea water and Hivis
sweeps as required . Penetration rates from 897m to 1660m averaged 97mhr . Below 2000m
penetration rates lowered significantly averaging 10 mhr . Hole angle reached its desired build

at 1374 m. At 2264 m the bit was pulled out of the hole due to the low penetration rate .

Bit # 5 a Reed EHP 51HLK was run in hole with the same BHA used previously . Three 8.0
drill collars were added and a jar replaced . This bit had a lower total flow area to reduce
possible washoutformation damage . From 2264 m to section TD at 2892 m the rate of
penetration averaged 14 mhr . The hole was displaced to gel with a 400 bbl KCL inhibited pill
spotted at bottom prior to running the 9 58 casing . The casing was run without incident and

was set and cemented at 2886 m .

On drilling out the 9 58 shoe track the well was displaced to SBM . A leak off test gave an
equivalent mud weight of 1.29 sg . The 8.5 BHA included a motor and FEWD which rotary
drilled to TD . Mud losses were encountered immediately on drilling into new formation and
continued to TD averaging 1020bblshr and rising to a maximum of 70 bblshr in the
Laminaria Sands . The losses continued after a number of attempts to prevent it with LCM
pilis and remained at 18 bblshr static . The first wireline logging run could not get past 3580 m
necessitating a wiper trip . During this trip more LCM was circulated and the mud weight was

reduced from 1.08 sg to 1.06 sg .

End of Well Report Corallina2 3

SperrySun Drilling Services

Formation Evaluation

Mud logging and geological evaluation for Corallina 2 commenced after setting the 13 38
casing and installing the riser and diverter at 890 m. Washed and unwashed samples were
collected at 5 m and 10 m intervals . Sampling intervals followed those specified in the drilling
program and only differed at the discretion of the Wellsite Geologist . Spot samples were
periodically taken to assist lithological interpretation . Mud samples were also collected at each

change of the mud system and prior to coring and wireline log runs .

Note that the intervals of characteristic lithology defined below are not intended to be
accurate with boundaries interpolated between samples where no significant change in
drilling parameters were observed . The lithological descriptions are done according to major

changes in lithology as recommended by the Wellsite Geologist .

The cuttings were described at the well site using a binocular microscope . The interpreted
lithology is based on cuttings and drilling parameters such as the rate of penetration weight

on bit background gas values and the gamma signal .

Corallina 2

Between 1560 and 2480 m the dominant lithology was Calcarenite with minor Caicilutite and
Argillaceaous Siltstone . The Calcarenite was generally white to yellowish grey moderately firm
to hard coarse to medium grained subangular to subrounded with common foraminifera
coral spicules and trace amounts of pyrite and glauconite .

The Calcilutite was white to light grey to pale yellow soft to firm and subblocky .

The Siltstone was light to medium greyish green soft dispersive variably calcareous and
contained trace to rare quantities of glauconite . Minor amounts of Dolomite were present at the
top of interval . It graded to Silty Claystone in lower part .

There were no shows in this interval .

SperrySun Drilling Services
Gas Ratio Plot .

A Gas Ratio plot can be found attached to this end of well report ( Appendix 7 ) . The following
description isa brief explanation to the use of different gas ratios applied to the Gas Ratio
Plot .

C1 Ratios ( CC CC CC CC ) . These display the fraction of each component
compared to the fraction of C. The ratios generally decrease with depth as more mature

sediments are encountered . Mature source rocks and hydrocarbon reservoirs show low ratios .
Gas Wetness Ratio ( GWR ) : CrCtCrC.JC x 100 . The GWR gives an indication of

maturity . It will generally increase with depth as the C1 fraction will represent a smaller part of
the total light HC .

Light to Heavy ratio ( LHR ) : ( C # C ) ( Cr # C # C . ) x 100 . The LHR is expected to decrease
with depth .

Oil Character qualifier ( OQC ) : ( C # C ) C. Under some circumstances high amounts of C
will mask the presence of oil . GWR and LHR could then be misinterpreted . In the presence of
oil C and C. will increase relative to C. and the OQC would increase .

Average Carbon Number ( CAN ) : C4 ( 2xC ) # ( 3xC ) H ( 4xC ) # ( 5xCs ) ( CrCtCrCrC . ) .

Note that C C and C are the least abundant components . Areas with low gas

readings will give unreliable ratios .

End of Well Report Corallina2 11

36 HOLE SECTION

36 HOLE DRILLED FROM 438.0 to 490.0m
30x20 CASING SET 484 m

No . BITS USED : 1

Corallina2 was spudded in at 438.0m RKB with a Varel L3A Tricone bit and drilled to
490.0m at an average penetration rate of 51 mhr . No problems were encountered during this

hole section . Returns were circulated to the seabed with an ROV used to monitor all subsea

operations . Seawater was used as the drilling fluid with PHG sweeps as required . It proved

impossible to get a survey with the DWD and instead a Totco was run giving an inclination of

2 degrees at 488m . When the 30720 casing was run a good seat was not achieved for the

hanger due to the excessive angle so it was pulled back and a 36 hole opening assembly

run into hole with DWD . After reaming down to TD the angle had been reduced to 0.4deg .

The casing was successfully set and cemented at 484m .

12 114 HOLE SECTION

12 14 HOLE DRILLED FROM 895 m TO 2892 m
9 58 Casing Set at 2886 m
No . BITS USED :2

Bit # 4 a Reed MHP 11G with 3 x 20327 and a 1032 jet nozzles total flow area of 0.997
was run in hole with FEWD and a SperryDrill Lobe 67 5 stage motor with a bend of 1.15 .
Cement was tagged at 845 m. After drilling through the cement float shoe and rathole two
meters of new formation were drilled and a Leak Off Test was performed with a result of 1.43
sg EMW . Drilling continued from 897m using sea water and Hivis sweeps as required .

Sliding began early at 968m due to problems in the past of building hole angle in this section .
The rates of penetration from 897m to1660m were high averaging 97mhr . Hole angle
reached the desired build of 29 ? at 1374m and was mentained throughout the section . No
difficulty was encountered steering in this hole section . From 1660m to 2000m the rate of
penetration averaged 48mvhr . Below 2000m penetration rates lowered significantly averaging
10mhr . At 2264m the bit was pulled out of hole due to the low penetration rate . Inclination at
this depth was 29.8 .

Bit # 5 an EHP51HLK was run in hole with a steerable bottom hole assembly as in the
previous bit run . However three 8.0 drill collars were added and a jar was replaced . This rock
bit had 2 x 1832 and a 1632 jet nozzles total flow area of 0.6933 . This allowed
increased jetting action on the formation being drilled for better cuttings clearance compared
to the previous bit . Drilling continued from 2264m using sea water and Hivis sweeps as
required . Rates of penetration averaged 14nvhr from 2264m to section TD at 2892m .
Fluctuating standpipe pressure was recorded below 2800m this was due to the Adjustable
Gauge Stabiliser starting to cycle . It had failed to cycle above this depth .The inclination at
section TD was 30.7 . The hole was then displaced with 1000 bbls of gel and a 400 bbl 1.15
s.g. KCL pill was spotted on bottom prior to the casing run .

The 9 58 Casing was run without incident . It was set and cemented at 2886m .

SperrySun Drilling Services

PRESSURE EVALUATION

While drilling Corallina2 the following factors were used in the detection of abnormal pore

pressures .

Ditch Gas : True background connection and trip gas are qualitative indicators of pore

pressure .
Hole conditions : Tightness drag and fill were used as qualitative indicators of pore pressure .

Cavings : Good indicator of underbalance where pore pressure is higher than hydrostatic
pressure of the drilling fluid .

Temperature : A qualitative indicator that can display increases of temperature on entering

over pressurised zones .

Modified Dc Exponent : The Modified drilling exponent ( Dxc ) was used to calculate pore
pressures in claystones using Eatons formula . Having established a trend line for normal pore
pressure ie . increasing with depth as the formation drillability decreases due to normal
compaction any cutbacks away from the trend line whilst drilling claystone indicate increasing
pore pressure

MLNDR : The modified Log Normalised Drill Rates is one of SperrySurs drilling models for
pore pressure prediction based on original work by Bourgoyne and Young ( 1974 ) . The
MLNDR predicts the behaviour of the insitu formation characteristics related to the borehole .
The observed and modified results can be equated to produce a value for pore pressure . The
plotted results show that in a normally compacted shale sequence MLNDR should decrease
with depth being directly proportional to ROP and thus an increase in MLNDR can be
associated with higher pore pressure

Post Drilling pressure evaluation tools : These were mainly wireline logs which determine
the formation bulk density sonic deep resistivity compensated neutron and gamma . An ascii
file data of these electric logs enabled the pressure engineer to come up with an Overburden
and Fracture Gradient Analysis Plot . This was done by inputting the bulk densities and
interval transit times ( deltaT ) on a spreadsheet which comprises overburden gradient and
effective overburden gradient calculations and Eatons formula for fracture gradient

calculation .

End of Well Report Corallina2 18

-----Page 161-----

SperrySun Drilling Services

Formation Pore Pressures

12114 Hole Section

The formation pore pressure for this section was estimated to be normal at 1.032 s.g. EMW .
Drilled gas as well as trip and connection gases were generally nil . There were no signs of
stressrelief consolidated cavings as the section mainly contained fractured carbonate rocks
with only minor argillaceous interbeds . Furthermore the bulk of the cuttings samples were
circulated together with the hivis pills due to frequent hole washouts . The modified D
Exponent and MLNDR values suggest normally increasing and decreasing trends
respectively with depth throughout this hole section . No significant cutbacks or abnormal
deflections were noted for those two pressure parameters . Realtime FEWD gamma and
resistivity were mainly low in the top hole section which was attributed to the high
intergranular porosity due to relative lack of cementation . Some slightly spiky and higher than
the average resistivity readings correspond to dolomite stringers and hard consolidated
calcarenites . From 1950 m MD ( 1856 m TVD ) to 2155 m MD ( 2035 m TVD ) the gamma trend
shifted to the right ( from 30 to 50 aapi ) suggesting increasing amounts of clay material while
the resistivity trace remained low at an average of 1.0 ohmmetre . A cleaner carbonate
interval with very rare argillaceous interbeds occurred from 2155 m to 2300 m MD ( 2162 m
TVD ) as shown by the cutback in the gamma trend . From 2300 m to 2323 m MD ( 2182 m
TVD ) the gamma had a positive deflection due to the occurrence of silty claystones . An
increase in the resistivity readings from 0.5 to 3 ohmmetres was noted from 2170 m ( 2049 m
TVD ) to 2290 m ( 2153 m TVD ) as depicted by good consolidation and compaction . A slight
resistivity cutback from 2290 m to 2545 m ( 2377 m TVD ) could be characterised as a slightly
less consolidated more porous carbonate interval . From 2545 m the resistivity trend of
values shifted to the right ( averaged from 1.1 to 4.0 ohmmetre ) which indicated a normally
increasing compaction trend . The gamma for the latter interval had a slight cutback though it
dropped even further at 2635 m ( 2456 m TVD ) from 50 to 20 aapi as the interbedded
argillaceous siltstones . and claystones decrease with depth . Realtime downhole
temperatures steadily increased with depth . In conclusion the foregoing parameters
discussed all indicate a normal formation pressure regime for the 1214 waterbased hole

section .

End of Well Report Corallina2 19

-----Page 162-----

SperrySun Drilling Services

8.5 Hole Section

Estimated normal formation pore pressures for this section ranged from 1.032 to a maximum
of 1.04 s.g. EMW on approach to well T.D . Background gas levels in this interval were
generally low averaging from a trace to 0.1 96. steadily increasing with depth . No connection
trip swab or surge gases were recorded . The equivalent circulating density of the mud while
drilling through this section was 1.07 s.g . The modified DExponent and MLNDR values were
slightiy erratic from 2892 m ( 2678 m TVD ) to 3120 m ( 2867 m TVD ) with a normal pore
pressure estimated at 1.035 s.g. EMW . Finally from 3120 m to 3555 m ( 3268 m TVD ) a slight
cutback in the Dxc with a corresponding increase in the MENDR trend was observed with the
pore pressure estimated to be normal between 1.037 to 1.04 s.g. EMW . This normal pore
pressure of 1.04 s.g. EMW prevailed till T.D . The MLNDR and DExponent values from 3555
m showed a decreasing and increasing trend respectively though these were triggered by a
significant drop in the rate of penetration ( from an average of 40 to 15 metres per hour ) on
approach to T.D . ( 3622 m MD3333 m TVD ) where the ROP decreased to 1.5 metres per
hour .

Realtime FEWD resistivity and gamma indicated a normal sediment compaction trend from
2892 m to 3125 m ( 2871 m TVD ) . A major cutback in resistivity with a simultaneous sharp
gamma increase at 3125 m marked a change in lithology from calcilutites to calcareous
claystones . A further positive gamma shift was encountered at 3203 m ( 2983 m TVD ) where
the readings were generally high and averaged from 70 to 120 aapi . The interval from 3203 to
3471 m ( 3188 m TVD ) was comprised of claystones with minor interbeds of calcilutites in the
top section . From 3471m the gamma plummeted down and revealed a fairly low trend whilst
a positive deflection in the resistivity trace from 2 to a maximum of 100 ohmmetres was
detected . Between 3484 m ( 3199 m TVD ) and 3531 m ( 3245 m TVD ) the resistivity readings
averaged around 80 ohmmetres . This interval was a predominantly 88arenaceous
hydrocarbonbearing sequence . A noted decline in the resistivity trend along with a
moderately sharp increase in the gamma was seen at 3531 m as indicated by the occurrence
of more porous slightiy less cemented water wet sands with occasional siltstone and
claystone interbeds . Realtime downhole temperatures followed a normal sediment
compaction trend with depth . The mud density had been raised from 1.07 to 1.08 s.g. which
resulted in continuous lost circulation downhole and also strongly suggests a normal pressure
regime . As defined by the afore mentioned pressure parameters there were no indications of
abnormal pore pressure within this section .

End of Well Report Corallina2 20

-----Page 163-----

SperrySun Drilling Services

FRACTURE AND OVERBURDEN GRADIENT

Spud to 12114 Hole Section

As shown in the Overburden and Fracture Gradient Analysis plot the overburden gradient
readings calculated from the mudline to 3622 m TD ( 3333 m TVD ) resembles an asymptotic
curve which is indicative of a normal sediment compaction trend . A leakoff test performed at
897 m MD ( 897 m TVD ) gave a fracture pressure gradient of 1.43 s.g. EMW which coincided
well with the calculated fracture gradient curve . The fracture gradient trend steadily increased
to 1.52 s.g. EMW at 1270 m MD ( 1259 m TVD ) but a cutback in the trend occurred below that
depth to a minimum of 1.415 s.g. EMW at 1280 m MD ( 1268 m TVD ) then went up to 1.523
s.g. EMW at 1300 m MD ( 1286 m TVD ) to follow the original trend . Once again it dropped to
142 s.g. EMW from 1310 m MD ( 1295 m TVD ) to 1320 m MD ( 1304 m TVD ) but eventually
followed the normal fracture pressure gradient trend at 1340 m MD ( 1322 m TVD ) . This was
attributed to the presence of dolomite interbedded with the calcarenites within that interval .
Further down the section there were more but small and fairly brief cutbacks in the fracture
gradient trend . One minor cutback seen between 1540 m MD ( 1497 m TVD ) and 1620 m
MD ( 1568 m TVD ) was due to the caicilutite interbeds then from 1630 m MD ( 1575 m TVD ) to
1740 m MD ( 1673 m TVD ) dolomite stringers were noted . The fracture gradient curve
continued its normal trend until 2100 m MD ( 1987 m TVD ) then it shifted to the left to minimum
pressure gradient of 1.4 s.g. EMW at 2150 m MD ( 2031 m TVD ) and then back to normal at
1.605 s.g. EMW at 2200 m MD ( 2075 m TVD ) . Again a minor leftward deflection occurred at
2210 m ( 2083 m TVD ) then it followed a steady vertical fracture pressure trend ( 1.486 to 1.49
s.g. EMW ) on approach to 2300 m MD ( 2162 m TVD ) . This interval corresponded to an
interbedded sequence of calcarenites calcilutites and argillaceous siltstone . Normal fracture
gradients extended down till 2500 m MD ( 2337 m TVD ) where another significant cutback was
observed from 1.6 to a minimum of 1.5 s.g. EMW and this gradient remained this tow till
2640 m MD ( 2461 m TVD ) . From 2640 m MD to 2892 m MD ( 2678 m TVD ) it generally
assumed a normal trend of values except for slight cutbacks in the lower part of the interval

where chert stringers were present .

The effective overburden is the difference between the overburden pressure and formation
balance gradient ( pore pressure ) . As illustrated in the plot the overburden pressures increase
with depth till 1214 hole T.D . whereas the formation balance gradient is pegged at 1.03
s.g. EMW . Based on this observation the overall trend of the effective overburden gradient is
closer to the pore pressure trend which indicates a normal formation pressure regime for this

hole section .

End of Well Report Corallina2 21

-----Page 164-----

SperrySun Drilling Services

8.5 Hole Section

From 2892 m ( 2678 m TVD ) the overburden gradient assumed an asymptotic curve on
approach to the total well depth also indicated a normal sediment compaction trend with
depth . The leakoff test at 2886 m MD ( 2745 m TVD ) which yielded a fracture pressure of 1.29
s.g. EMW was lower than the calculated value on the fracture gradient curve which showed
1.58 s.g. EMW . This could be due to presence of a local fault or fracture . Two minor cutbacks
in the fracture gradient curve were noted and these were : from 2975 m MD ( 2746 m TVD ) to
2995 m MD ( 2763 m TVD ) with values decreasing from 1.59 to 1.48 s.g. EMW and from 3090
m MD ( 2841 m TVD ) to 3115 m MD ( 2862 m TVD ) with values decreasing from 1.59 to 1.37
s.g. EMW . The normal fracture gradients averaged from 1.57 to 1.59 s.g. EMW . Fracture
gradient values ranged from 1.33 to 1.37 s.g. EMW from 3160 m MD ( 2901 m TVD ) to 3480 m
MD ( 3195 m TVD ) which was a major cutback interval . This conformed with a change in
lithology from carbonates to predominantiy claystones . From 3480 to 3500 m MD ( 3215 m
TVD ) the fracture gradient trend was steady and ranged from 1.13 to 1.15 s.g. EMW . This
interval was predominantly an arenaceous sequence with minor claystone interbeds . Finally
from 3530 m MD ( 3243 m TVD ) to the total depth of 3622 m MD ( 3333 m TVD ) the fracture
gradient curve followed a normal trend ranging from 1.13 to 1.16 s.g. EMW . This interval was
also predominantly arenaceous though there was quite a difference in rock matrix and bulk

densities between the two intervals which contributed to such contrast in fracture pressures .
Both the overburden pressures and formation balance gradient values increased with depth .

With reference to the effective overburden gradient curve it is still closer to the pore pressure

trend which again defines a normally pressured 812 hole section .

End of Well Report Corallina2 22

2 . Operational Overview

Job Number : AUFE80009 Well : Corallina2 MWD DIilling Report

-----Page 191-----

Woodside

LA ULAN

Operational Overview

The well was drilled using the semisubmersible rig Sedco 703 . Sperry Sun Drilling Services were contracted to
provide Measurement While Drilling ( MWD ) services from surface to TD .

In the 36 and 1712 sections a directional only positive pulse tool was run to ensure the well remained
vertical .

In the 1214 hole section a negative pulse Formation Evaluation While Drilling ( FEWD ) tool run to help in
the accurate determination of formation tops . A Drillstring Dynamics Sensor was also run to analyse downhole
vibration in an attempt to alleviate possible BHA damage or failure . Sperry Suns data detection efficiency was
approximately 9846 realtime and 10096 recorded . Total depth of the 1214 was 2892m MDRT .

A similar suite of tools was run in the 812 Open Hole Section the primary objective being to pick the top of
the reservoir . Sperry Suns data detection efficiency was approximately 9896 realtime and 10046 recorded .

The well was successfully drilled to a final TD of 3622.28m MDRT ( 3332.8m TVDRT ) .

5 . Vibration Report

Job Number : AUFE80009 Well : Corallina2 MWD Iilling Report

-----Page 202-----

Woodside

LALABAS P LLANA

Sensor Description :

SperrySuns Drilling Dynamic Sensor ( DDS ) consists of three mutually orthogonal accelerometers rigidly
mounted on the Gamma Ray insert . These accelerometers measure the downhole shock and vibration on three
independent circuits Average Peak and Instantaneous . The accelerometers and electronics have a frequency
response of 5000 Hz and the range is from O to 250 Gs . The sensor has its own microprocessor and 512K
RAM for data processing and storage .

Average Circuit :

The average circuit measures the vibration data by taking the average acceleration value over a user defined
sample period . The average data will detect the low frequency vibrations . Low frequency vibrations have the
highest energies and are the most destructive .

Peak Circuit :

The peak circuit measures and records the highest vibration detected during the sample period . The peak data is
useful in detecting high frequency vibrations that occur during bit whirl BHA whirl and bit bounce .

Instantaneous Circuit :

The Instantaneous Circuit samples at a user defined rate of 1000 to 5000 Hz . The user defines a threshold and a
block size for the Burst data . When the threshold is exceeded the sensor rapidly records the data until the
block is filled . The Burst data is used for frequency analysis . The frequency of the vibration data can be
determined by performing a Fast Fourier Transform on the burst data . Burst data is generally sampled at 1000
Hz with a Block size was 8 Kb and a2 g average lateral vibration threshold .

Background :

Downhole vibration can not be avoided . Most of the time low level vibration is harmless . However extreme
downhole vibration can be very destructive . Some problems associated with severe vibration are drillstring
failure premature bit failure top drive stalling well bore damage MWD tool failures and inefficient drilling .

The primary source of drillstring vibration is the interaction by the bit and drill string to the well bore . The
drilistring response to these forces are intricate and will not be discussed in this report The DDS sensor can
provide useful data to improve drilling efficiency by minimising destructive downhole excitations . To
accomplish this requires an understanding of the physics of downhole vibration .

PA Z344 ? ? ? RAHA tt # Qdd dd ( KK ( Q ZING aaa
Job Number : AUFE80009 Well : Corallina2 MWD Irilling Report

-----Page 203-----

Vibration Classification :

Vibration can be induced on three components of motion . These components are axial torsional and lateral .
Axial motion is motion along the longitudinal axis of the drillstring . Torsional is motion along the rotational
axis of the drillstring and lateral is motion along the axis perpendicular to the drillstring . There are several
mechanisms which can induce destructive downhole vibration . Some of these mechanisms are

Stickslip : Inconsistent bit rotation in which the bit slows or stops momentarily building up torque and
subsequently spins free . Stickslip can cause severe damage to PDC bits and drillstring twistoffs . Stickslip is
low frequency vibration ( 41 Hz ) and can be detected by the separation of the average X and average Y data
values . Stickslip motion generally occurs with PDC bits .

Bit Bounce : Bit bounce is caused by large weight on bit fluctuations which often occurs when drilling with
tricone bits in hard formations with large amounts of weight on bit . These fluctuations can cause premature bit
failure and BHA damage . Bit bounce vibrations are higher frequency accelerations ( 110 Hz ) and can be
detected by the presence of high peak Z values .

Bit Whirl : Bit whirl is defined as eccentric rotation around a point other than the geometric centre of the bit .
This mechanism instigates high frequency lateral and torsional vibration . Bit whirl can cause rapid failure of
PDC bits .

BHA Whirl : BHA whirl is when components of the BHA such as stabilisers tool joints etc . walk around the
well bore in an eccentric non centralised path . BHA whirl induces high frequency lateral and rotational
vibrations . This can cause damage to the BHA components .

Modal Coupling : ls caused by the combination of any of the above vibration modes and specifically creates
very high lateral vibrations . The symptoms and affects of modal coupling can be any combination of bit damage
MWD failures wash outs and twists offs due to tool joint fatigue collar and stabiliser wear .

.Severity of vibration indicated by DDS



Vibration Detection :

SperrySun MWD has the capability of transmitting any combination of average and peak data for all three
axiss of the sensor . Average difference between the X and Y axis is used to indicate the presence of stickslip
motion . Bit bounce is determined by high peak Z axis readings . Bit or BHA whirl can be identified by high
peak X and Y readings medium to high average X and Y readings where the difference between average X and
Y is small . Lateral shocks can be identified by high peak X and Y with the average X and Y being low . Average
X and peak Y indicated the occurrence of lateral collisions . Modal coupling can be identified by high Peak X Y
and Z axis vibration the average vibrations may still be low due to the chaotic nature of the vibration .

Job Number : AUFE80009 Well : Corallina2 MWD Drilling Report

-----Page 204-----

Woodside

Results :

1214 Section

This section was drilled in two bit runs all of which were failure free . Both of these runs utilised Sperry Suns
Steerable Sperrydrill Motors for performance optimisation . At the end of each run 10026 of the recorded data
was recovered . While drilling the 12 4 Open Hole Section changes were made to the WOB and RPM to
alleviate the vibrations usually encountered when drilling through chert .

MWD Run 4 895m2264m MD

Data transmitted PX PY PZ AY
Bit used RC ( MHP11G ) grading 23WTAE116OCPR
Parameters used : WOB : 1050 klbs

RPM : 1090

ROP : 33.16 mhr

Minimal vibrations were encountered on this run . RPM and WOB were altered on a few occasions and the
direct result from these was an instantaneous decrease in downhole vibrations . Overall the MWD tool
performed well during the whole run .

MWD Run 5 2264m2892m MD

Data transmitted # PX PY PZ AX AY
Bit used RC ( EHP5ILK ) grading 13BTOE116WTTD
Parameters used : WOB : 1540 kibs

RPM : 7090

ROP : 13.55 mhr

During this run the transmitted levels of PX and PY values were of a low to medium nature . Changes to the
drilling parameters were made to increase drilling performance for this section . Chert was recorded from 2655 to
2890 mRT ( 10 2076 chert from 2785 2820 mRT ) but did not make any significant impact on drilling
operations . 8 Vibrations were significantly low for the section . Recorded data was 10096 and realtime
transmissions rate was also relatively high .

812 Section

A single MWD nun for the 8 72 section produced 9596 realtime and 10026 recorded data thus fulfilling their
objectives required by Woodside . Steerable string assemblies were used in order to maintain build angle for this
directional well . Minimal vibrations were emanated within the section since corrective drilling parameters were
strictly adhered to by Woodside in order to optimise drilling performance and reduce the likelihood of damage
to the BHA .

o AA AA AS SSS SS SS AS AASA AASA
Job Number : AUFE80009 Well : Corallina2 MWD DIilling Report

-----Page 205-----

Woodside

MWD Run 6 2892m3622.28m MD

Data transmitted PX PY PZ AX AY AZ
Bit used PDC ( FM2743 ) grading 45ROSX116WTTD
Parameters used : WOB : 530 klbs

RPM : 110120

ROP : 15.76 mhr

This run exhibited primarily low vibrations . Favourable geological application and optimal drilling parameters
contributed to a smooth and controlled drilling performance in order to select an ideal TD point . Where
vibrations were evident drilling parameters were altered on a few occasions and the direct result was an
instantaneous decrease in downhole vibrations . Overall the FEWD tool achieved its fundamental objective
delivering for Woodside vital downhole data for future analyses .

Recommendations

Monitoring real time vibrations proved to be advantageous in avoiding BHA and bit damage during Corallina2
drilling phase . Both the 12 14 and 8 12 hole sections were drilled in three separate MWD runs each of which
was failure free . This can be partly attributed to the monitoring system . Harder formations and debilitating bit
conditions proved to be the points of maximum vibration .

During the drilling of Corallina2 it was seen as more practical to let the vibrations remain in the low to medium

range in order to maximise penetration rates . Sperry Sun proposed that the current attention to DDS data while
drilling be maintained in order to prevent vibration related BHA damage .

-----Page 221-----

Introduction

WESTERN ATLAS LOGGING SERVICES conducted a Zero Offset VSP and Velocity
Checkshot Survey for WOODSIDE OFFSHORE PETROLEUM in the CORALLINA2
well located in Offshore Australia . The wireline service for this survey was also provided
by WESTERN ATLAS LOGGING SERVICES .

The survey was conducted in one run . The survey lasting approximately 8 hour 12
minutes . The survey began at 13:23 hours on April 15th 1998 and was completed
at 21:35 in the same day . Field Observers Logs for this run are included in
Enclosure 1 of this report .

During the velocity checkshot survey the reference measurement is the Lowest
Astronomical Tide ( LAT ) as datum and was not Mean Sea Level which is varies
from LAT . The gun depth was 5.00 meters below sea level . Due to sea level varies
from datum the gun depth need to be corrected to datum of LAT using the tidal
correction data supplied by the client .

All measured depths are referenced to the Kelly Bushing ( KB ) elevation of 30.5 meters
above LAT . The water depth at the wellhead was 408.3 meters below KB . The data for
all runs consisted of 229 files and was gathered at 185 depth levels between the depths
of 735 and 3566 meters measured depth below KB .

At the time of the survey the well had been drilled to a measured depth of 3622.3 meter
( KB ) . The borehole was reported as a deviated well .

Logging Services

-----Page 222-----

Field Procedure

DOWNHOLE SEISMIC SERVICES ( DSS ) crew and equipment arrived at the well on
April 12 1998 . All equipment was tested on site prior to the survey . DSS employed
standard techniques for the Zero Offset VSP and Velocity Checkshot Survey .

The energy source used for this survey were two 70 cu inch sleeve guns ( total energy
source was 140 cu inch ) . The source location was 63 M N351.49E degree from the
welihead with gun depth was 5.0 meter below sea level . The water depth at the
wellhead was 408.3 meter below KB . The nomenclature chart and wellbore illustration
are shown in Figures 1 and Enclosure 1B ( Section 5 and Section 6 ) .

With the start of the survey the wireline depth sensor was zeroed at the Kelly Bushing
( KB ) elevation . The geophone tool was stopped going into the borehole to check all
equipment performance .

In order to monitor the consistency of the depth measuring device and to check for any
cable stretch shots were taken as the tool descended the borehole at some interval
depths between of 735 795 1110 1170 2010 2070 and 3060 3120 meter . The
geophone tool was then lowered to a depth of 3566 meter below KB . Recording of the
data commenced at that depth and proceeded as the geophone was raised to shallower
depths . The shallowest depth level occupied was 735 meter ( K.B. ) . In this survey the
checkshot levels were recorded between depths of 735 and 3566 meters .

At each downhole station the wireline cable was stopped and the surface controlled
motor driven arm was activated to lock the geophone tool to the borehole wall . On
completion of recording for a depth level the wirelines cable slack was removed the
locking arm retracted and the tool moved to the next depth level . An average of 5 shots
were taken at each depth level and data was recorded with a 1 msec sample rate and a
record length of 4 seconds .

LAT
WESTERN
ATLAS

Logging Services

-----Page 223-----

DATA PROCESSING AND INTERPRETATION

First Break Picking

The digital data was demultiplexed and displayed . All shots per level were edited and
summed to produce a stacked digital record arranged according to increasing depth .
First break times were picked from the first break on the gun hydrophone signal to the
first break on the geophone signal . The first break picking was performed manually and
no filtering were applied . A display of the data for the velocity checkshot survey is
included in the back of this report in Enclosure 2 .

For the velocity survey calculations record quality was assigned according to the
following scale :

Good ( G ) No extraneous disturbance clear sharp high
amplitude first break .
Fair ( F ) inferior to G in one or more respects ( mentioned
above ) but quite dependable to within # 1.5 to 2
. msec .
Poor ( P ) Definitely inferior to Fi : a weak break or low

signaltonoise ratio difficult to judge to within # 2
to 3 msec but no doubt as to its authenticity .

Estimated ( E ) Barely usable perhaps a matter of doubt as to its
authenticity particularly at shallow levels where
precursory energy is dominant .

Not Usable ( NU ) First arrival not distinguishable usually due to
poor tool coupling or due to poor signaltonoise
ratio .

The recorded measured depths and times of the check levels have been affected by
the borehole deviation . These have been corrected to the vertical using the
deviation data supplied by the client . The corrected values have been used
throughout the calculations .

A total of 185 checkshot levels were recorded between depths of 735 and 3566 meters
measured depths below KB . The first arrivals of the checkshot at depths of 735 750
765 780 795 885 and 900 were affected by casing ringing . Their first arrival could not
be obtained these checkshot levels have therefore been omitted from the final Velocity
Survey Computations . The remaining data is of good quality with well defined first break .
A total of 178 checkshot levels between depths of 915 3566 meter have been used in
the Final Velocity Survey Computations .

Waw
WESTERN
ATLAS

Logging Services

-----Page 224-----

Velocity Survey Processing

Due to sea level varies from the datum of LAT as the tidal effects the gun depths have
been corrected from this effect using the Tidal Information Table supplied by the client .

The observed first break times were converted to vertical times using the cosine
correction as the corrected vertical time from the gun to the well geophone . The time
correction from gun to datum is performed by dividing the depth ( gun depth # depth
between gun to hydrophone ) with water velocity ( 1500 metersec. ) . This time correction
from gun to datum was then added to the corrected vertical time from the gun to the well
geophone as the corrected vertical traveltime between datum and well geophone .
These corrections can be seen in the Time Depth Information Table sheet ( Section
4 )

Final calculations timedepth summary and a detailed velocity listing are also includer
in Section 4 . The final timedepth and averagelinterval velocity curves are included as
Enclosure 3 .

All nomenclature relating to table headings in section 4 can be located on Figure 1
section 5 .

Acoustic Log

A continuous Acoustic log was provided by WOODSIDE OFFSHORE PETROLEUM .
The logs have been edited for any remaining noise spikes and have been reintegrated
prior to calibration . Any gaps between different Acoustic runs have been modeled at the
general velocity of the adjacent of log .

Acoustic Log Calibration

The calibration curves are well controlled by the check shot data . The shifts have been
formulated to change at the same formations on the calibration curve . There is some
scatter about the calibration curve however it is considered unrealistic to follow the
individual shifts implied by these points and so the general trend has been chosen .

The calibration is considered to be the best interpretation of the available data .

The calibration results are tabulated at 10 meter and 2 msec . intervals below datum and
are included in Section 4 . Plots of the drift curves before and after calibration are
included as Figures 2 and 3 ( Section 5 ) . A plot of the original and calibrated velocity log
are included as Enclosure 4 .

JAN
WESTERN
ATLAS

Logging Services

-----Page 225-----

Synthetic Seismogram

The calibrated Acoustic log has been used along with the Density log in the production
of the Synthetic Seismogram . Synthetic Seismograms were generated using Bandpass
wavelets zero and minimum phase as requested by the client both polarities of :

5107080 Hz : 510 6070 Hz : 5 10 5060 Hz and 5 10 4050 Hz

The Synthetic Seismograms are plotted with the Interval Velocity Log the Density Log
Acoustic Impedance Log Calibrated Acoustic Log Uncalibrated Acoustic Log Gamma
Ray Log Resistivity Log Deep Neutron Porosity Caliper Transmission Loss and the
Reflectivity Series at scales of 10 cm.sec and 20 cmsec ( as requested by the client )
these are included as Enclosure 5A to 5D respectively ( Section 6 ) .

VSP Processing Zero Offset VSP

A total of 173 checkshot levels between depths of 990 and 3566 meters below KB have
been used in the final VSP data processing .

The summed data were corrected to compensate for amplitude decay due to spherical
divergence using an exponential gain function of T11.5 ( where T is the recorded time ) .
A display of the gained total wavefield is included in Enclosure 6A .

The downgoing waves were flattened using the first arrival times . Each trace was cross
correlated with a selected reference trace using a time window around the first arrival
and the first arrival times were subsequently shifted to ensure maximum coherency of
the downgoing waves . A fifteen points median filter was applied to the total wavefield to
pass the flattened downgoing waves . A display of the flattened downgoing waves is
included in the back of this report ( Enclosure 6A ) . These downgoing waves were then
subtracted from the total wavefield to provide the upcoming waves this upcoming waves
were then shifted to twoway time . A five point median filter was applied to the flattened
upwaves in order to suppress noise . The data was then bandpass filtered with an
optimum filter of 510 70 100 hz to include the maximum frequency content of the data
this data is displayed as Undeconvolved Enhanced Upwaves .

Individual deconvolution operators were designed using 1200 msec . of the Downgoing
waveform for each depth level to shape the wavetrain to a spike . These operators were
then applied to the corresponding upcoming waves . The deconvolution results were
then filtered using a BPF of 510 70100 Hz trapezoid and then a nine points median
filter was applied to enhance the data as Deconvolved Enhanced Upwaves or Final
Upwaves . A display of Deconvolved Enhanced Upwaves is included in the back of this
report in Enclosure 6A .

Logging Services

-----Page 226-----

6

A corridor was defined close to the time of the first arrivals and a corridor stack was
generated a display of the corridor muted window raw corridor stack and filtered
corridor stack is included in the back of this report in Enclosure 6B and 6C .

VSP Displays ( Enclosure 6A ) has been included showing the Total Wavefield
Downgoing Wavefield Undeconvolved Enhanced Upwaves Deconvolved Unenhanced
Upwaves Deconvolved Enhanced Upwaves . Corridor Stack display showing Corridor
Muted Window Corridor Stack Raw and Filtered ( with both polarities ) .

VSP CDP Transformation

A time variant depth model was generated from the Checkshot data . The deconvolved
Upwaves were input into the VSPCDP transform program . After specifying the survey
ray tracing was carried out on the input depth model to map the direct arrivel times .
These times were then compared to the recorded direct arrival times in order to confirr
the model was correct .

After the confirmation of the model the transformation coordinates were used to map
the Upcoming Pwaves of the VSP data into CDP offset and twoway time . A subsurface
bin width of 10 meter was selected to vertically sum the traces that fell within the
boundaries of the specified bins .

Display of the transformation in time are included in the back of the report in Enclosure
8A and 8B .

WOODSIDE CORALLINA No . 2 WELL

@ ( 356070360005m )

PALYNOLOGICAL REPORT BASIC DATA

@ A report prepared for
Woodside Offshore Petroleum October 25 1998

-----Page 299-----

a

BASIC DATA

INTRODUCTION

Palynological preparations from six ( 6 ) ditch cuttings samples from Woodside Corallina2 well were examined .
Organic yields data were not recorded due to the high proportions of lost circulation material in the cuttings .
Probable in situ organic yields were generally low resulting in diluted palynomorph concentrations . The state
of preservation of the palynomorphs ranged from very poor to tair . Distribution of selected taxa are illustrated
on Table 3 .

The samples were processed by Laola Pty Ltd in Perth . The standard of the preparations was generally fair

although the proportions of LCM was a problem .
